Question 649 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 12-years old girl is brought by her parents to Ophthalmology OPD. According to the parents, the patient has congenital cataracts since birth. What is the most important complication of untreated congenital cataracts?

Options:
  a. Retinal detachment
  b. Corneal ulcer
✓ c. Amblyopia
  d. Optic disc atrophy
  e. Lens subluxation

Explanation:
The most critical complication of untreated congenital cataract is Amblyopia (lazy eye) due to visual deprivation during the critical period of development.

================================================================================
Question 650 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
An elderly patient is presented with a mass on upper lateral eye lid margin, the mass central ulceration and raised edged, the most likely diagnosis could be:

Options:
  Chalazion
  Stye
  Lacrimal gland inflammation
✓ BCC

Explanation:
A mass on the eyelid margin with central ulceration and raised, rolled edges (often described as 'pearly' with telangiectatic vessels) is the classic clinical presentation of basal cell carcinoma (BCC), which is the most common malignant eyelid tumor, especially in elderly, sun-exposed individuals.

Question 651 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A patient is presented with upper eye dropping after cataract surgery, the most likely type of ptosis is:

Options:
✓ Aponeurotic
  Myogenic
  Mechanical
  Neurogenic

Explanation:
Aponeurotic ptosis, specifically post-surgical aponeurotic ptosis, is the most common type of upper eyelid drooping that occurs after cataract surgery. It is caused by dehiscence, stretching, or disinsertion of the levator aponeurosis during or after the surgical procedure.

Question 652 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Chalazion is:

Options:
  Acute suppurative inflammation of
✓ Chronic granulomatous inflammation of Meibomian gland
  Retention cyst of Meibomian gland
  Neoplasm of the Meibomian glands

Explanation:
A chalazion is a chronic, sterile, lipogranulomatous inflammation of the meibomian gland. It develops when the duct of a meibomian gland becomes obstructed, leading to the leakage of lipid contents into the surrounding eyelid tissue, triggering a granulomatous inflammatory response.

================================================================================
Question 653 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A patient has upper lid trichiasis with history of chronic eye irritation. The most common Causes are:

Options:
  Stye
✓ Trachoma
  Infected Chalazion
  Spring catarrh

Explanation:
Trichiasis, which is the misdirection of eyelashes to rub against the cornea, is often caused by chronic inflammation and scarring of the eyelid margin. Trachoma, a chronic chlamydial conjunctivitis, is a leading cause of cicatricial (scarring) changes in the conjunctiva and eyelids, resulting in entropion and subsequent trichiasis.

================================================================================
Question 654 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A mother noticed a mucopurulent discharge from the puncta of her 3 months old son. There is a history of watering from his eye. Which of the following is an appropriate treatment:

Options:
  Syringing
  Probing with syringing
✓ Sac massage with local antibiotic
  DCR surgery

Explanation:
In a 3-month-old infant with watering and mucopurulent discharge from the puncta, indicating congenital nasolacrimal duct obstruction, the initial and most appropriate treatment is conservative management. This includes lacrimal sac massage (Crigler massage) to encourage opening of the duct and topical broad-spectrum antibiotics to manage any secondary infection.

================================================================================
Question 655 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Nasolacrimal ducts opens into the:

Options:
✓ Inferior meatus
  Superior meatus
  Lacrimal duct
  Conjunctival sac

Explanation:
The nasolacrimal duct drains tears from the lacrimal sac into the nasal cavity, specifically opening into the inferior meatus of the nose, beneath the inferior turbinate.

================================================================================
Question 656 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Lacrimal puncta is present on the:

Options:
✓ Medial side
  Lateral side
  superior fornix
  Inferior fornix

Explanation:
The lacrimal puncta are small openings located on the medial (nasal) side of the upper and lower eyelids, near the inner canthus. They collect tears from the conjunctival sac and drain them into the lacrimal canaliculi.

================================================================================
Question 657 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Phlycten is due to:

Options:
✓ Endogenous allergy
  Exogenous allergy
  Degeneration
  None of above

Explanation:
A phlycten is a manifestation of phlyctenular keratoconjunctivitis, which is a type IV hypersensitivity (delayed-type) reaction to endogenous microbial proteins, most commonly from *Staphylococcus aureus* or *Mycobacterium tuberculosis*.

================================================================================
Question 658 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A young child suffering from fever and sore throat began to complain of lacrimation. On examination, follicles were found in the lower palpebral conjunctiva with tender preauricular lymph nodes. The most probable diagnosis is:

Options:
  Trachoma
  Staphylococcal conjunctivitis
✓ Adenoviral conjunctivitis
  Phlyctenular conjunctivitis

Explanation:
The combination of fever, sore throat (pharyngitis), and follicular conjunctivitis with tender preauricular lymphadenopathy is the classic triad of pharyngoconjunctival fever, which is caused by Adenovirus (types 3, 7).

================================================================================
Question 659 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A young boy presented in emergency with watering and photophobia in the right eye. Which test is appropriate:

Options:
  Schirmer Test
  Tear breakup time
  Rose Bengal testing
✓ Flouroscine staining

Explanation:
Watering and photophobia in a young boy strongly suggest a corneal abrasion or foreign body. Fluorescein staining is the standard and most appropriate test to visualize corneal epithelial defects, which will stain green under cobalt blue light.

================================================================================
Question 660 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 12 year old boy receiving long term treatment for spring catarrh, developed defective vision in both Eyes. The likely cause is:

Options:
✓ Posterior Subcapsular cataract
  Retinopathy of prematurity
  Optic neuritis
  Vitreous hemorrhage

Explanation:
Spring catarrh (Vernal Keratoconjunctivitis) is often treated with topical corticosteroids. Long-term use of steroids is a well-known risk factor for developing posterior subcapsular cataracts, as well as steroid-induced glaucoma.

================================================================================
Question 661 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A patient in slit lamp examination shows hypopyon in anterior chamber after trauma, which is:

Options:
✓ Pus in anterior chamber
  Cells in anterior chamber
  Protein in anterior chamber
  Blood in anterior chamber
  Foreign body in anterior chamber

Explanation:
Hypopyon is defined as the accumulation of pus (leukocytes/white blood cells) in the anterior chamber of the eye, settling inferiorly due to gravity. It is a sign of severe anterior segment inflammation, often due to corneal ulcer or endophthalmitis.

================================================================================
Question 662 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A patient is presented with dendritic corneal ulcer and severe pain and having a history of contact lens wear, which organism is most likely responsible for the condition:

Options:
  Herpes simplex
✓ Acanthamoeba
  Candida
  Both a and b

Explanation:
While dendritic ulcers are classic for Herpes Simplex, *Acanthamoeba* keratitis (associated strongly with contact lens wear) can present with dendriform or pseudo-dendritic epithelial lesions in the early stages. Crucially, *Acanthamoeba* is known for causing disproportionately severe pain out of proportion to clinical signs. The combination of contact lens wear, severe pain, and a dendriform lesion should raise high suspicion for *Acanthamoeba*.

================================================================================
Question 663 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In band keratopathy which corneal layer is involved:

Options:
✓ Bowmen's layer
  Epithelium layer
  Endothelium layer
  None of these

Explanation:
Band keratopathy involves the deposition of calcium salts primarily in the Bowman's layer of the cornea, often extending into the anterior stroma and basement membrane of the epithelium.

================================================================================
Question 664 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In keratoconus the cornea becomes:

Options:
  Cone shaped
  Spherical shape
  Thin at the center
✓ Both a and c

Explanation:
Keratoconus is a progressive non-inflammatory ectatic disorder where the cornea undergoes thinning (usually central or paracentral) and protrudes into a conical shape. Thus, both cone shape and thinning are correct.

================================================================================
Question 665 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The color of fluorescein staining in corneal ulcer is:

Options:
  Yellow
  Blue
✓ Green
  Red

Explanation:
Fluorescein dye stains areas of corneal epithelial loss (such as an ulcer). When viewed under cobalt blue light, the stained area fluoresces a bright green color.

================================================================================
Question 666 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Bandage of the eyes is contraindicated in:

Options:
  Corneal abrasion
  Bacterial corneal ulcer
✓ Mucopurulent conjunctivitis
  After glaucoma surgery

Explanation:
Bandaging or patching the eye is contraindicated in purulent or mucopurulent conjunctivitis (and infected corneal ulcers) because the patch retains discharge, increases the temperature of the eye, and creates an incubator-like environment that promotes bacterial growth.

================================================================================
Question 667 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Normal radius of curvature of posterior corneal surface is:

Options:
  7.8mm
✓ 6.8mm
  7.9mm
  6.0mm

Explanation:
The cornea is steeper posteriorly than anteriorly. The average radius of curvature of the anterior corneal surface is about 7.8 mm, while the posterior surface is approximately 6.5 mm to 6.8 mm.

================================================================================
Question 668 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Hebert's pits are seen in:

Options:
✓ Trachoma
  Herpetic conjunctivitis
  Ophthalmia neonatorum
  Spring catarrh

Explanation:
Herbert's pits are shallow, scarred depressions at the limbus, which are the sequelae of resolved limbal follicles in Trachoma. They are a pathognomonic sign of past trachoma infection.

================================================================================
Question 669 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The incision size in phacoemulsification is;

Options:
  1mm
✓ 3mm
  5mm
  7mm

Explanation:
Standard phacoemulsification incisions typically range from 2.2 mm to 3.2 mm. Therefore, 3mm is the closest and most appropriate standard answer for a clear corneal phaco incision.

================================================================================
Question 670 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Evisceration is:

Options:
  Excision of the entire eyeball
✓ Excision of all the inner contents of the eye ball includ the uveal tissue
  Photocoagulation of retina
  Removal of orbit contents

Explanation:
Evisceration is the surgical removal of the intraocular contents (uvea, lens, retina, vitreous) while leaving the sclera (scleral shell) and extraocular muscles intact. Excision of the entire eyeball is enucleation.

================================================================================
Question 671 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Pseudophakia is the loss of:

Options:
✓ Accommodation
  Conversion
  Saccadic eye movements
  Contrast sensitivity

Explanation:
Pseudophakia refers to the state of having an artificial intraocular lens (IOL) implanted after cataract removal. Standard monofocal IOLs do not can change shape like the natural crystalline lens, leading to a complete loss of accommodation (the ability to focus at different distances).

================================================================================
Question 672 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The treatment of choice for the eye in angle closure glaucoma is:

Options:
  Surgical peripheral iridectomy
✓ Yag laser iridotomy
  Trabeculotomy
  Trabeculectomy

Explanation:
Nd:YAG laser peripheral iridotomy (LPI) is the definitive first-line treatment for primary angle closure (and the fellow eye). It creates a hole in the iris to relieve pupillary block.

================================================================================
Question 673 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Tropical Atropine is contraindicated in:

Options:
  Retinoscopy in children
  Iridocyclitis
  Corneal ulcer
✓ Primary angle closure glaucoma

Explanation:
Atropine is a mydriatic (dilates the pupil). In eyes with narrow angles (predisposed to angle closure), dilation can crowd the angle further and precipitate an acute attack of angle closure glaucoma.

================================================================================
Question 674 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Neovascular glaucoma follows:

Options:
✓ Thrombosis of central retinal vein
  Acute congestive glaucoma
  Staphylococcal infection
  Hypertension

Explanation:
Neovascular glaucoma (NVG) is a secondary glaucoma caused by retinal ischemia. Ischemic Central Retinal Vein Occlusion (CRVO) is a major cause, often leading to '90-day glaucoma' due to VEGF release and new vessel formation in the angle.

================================================================================
Question 675 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A month-old baby is brought with complaints of photophobia and watering. Clinical examinations show Normal tear passages and clear but large cornea. the most likely diagnosis is:

Options:
  Congenital dacryocystitis
  Interstitial keratitis
  Keratoconus
✓ Buphthalmos

Explanation:
The triad of epiphora (watering), photophobia, and blepharospasm in an infant, combined with large corneas (megalocornea/buphthalmos) is classic for Primary Congenital Glaucoma.

================================================================================
Question 676 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
You have been referred a case of open angle glaucoma. Which of the following would be an important Point in diagnosing the case:

Options:
  Shallow anterior chamber
✓ optic disc cupping
  Narrow angle
  Visual acuity and refractive error

Explanation:
In open-angle glaucoma, the angle is open (ruling out shallow AC/narrow angle). Visual acuity is often preserved until late. The hallmark diagnostic sign is glaucomatous optic neuropathy, characterized by optic disc cupping (increased cup-to-disc ratio).

================================================================================
Question 677 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
When ciliary muscle contracts, it results into:

Options:
  Increase tension on zonular fibers
  Decrease tension on zonular fibers
  Decrease tension on the lens
✓ Both b and c

Explanation:
Contraction of the ciliary muscle moves the ciliary body inward/forward. This relaxes the zonular fibers (decreases tension), allowing the lens to become more spherical (increase curvature) for accommodation. So, it decreases tension on zonules and allows the lens capsule to mold the lens.

================================================================================
Question 678 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Normal intra ocular pressure in human eye is:

Options:
✓ 10_21 mmhg
  16-25 mmhg
  13-22 mmhg
  9-19 mmhg

Explanation:
The statistically normal range for intraocular pressure is typically cited as 10 to 21 mmHg.

Question 679 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A one month old baby is brought with complaints of photophobia and watering. Clinical examination Shows normal tear passages and clear but large Cornea. The most likely diagnosis is:

Options:
  Congenital dacryocystitis
  Interstitial keratitis
  Keratoconus
✓ Buphthalmos

Explanation:
Duplicate question. Buphthalmos (Congenital Glaucoma) presents with large corneas, photophobia, and watering.

Question 680 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Aqueous humour formation is the function of:

Options:
  Ciliary muscle
✓ Ciliary process
  Pigmented epithelium
  Both b and c

Explanation:
Aqueous humor is produced by the non-pigmented epithelium of the ciliary processes (part of the ciliary body) via active secretion.

================================================================================
Question 681 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Ciliary body helps in:

Options:
  Maintaining structure of eye ball
  Focusing ability of eye ball
  Crystalline lens accommodation
✓ All of the above

Explanation:
The ciliary body produces aqueous humor (maintaining structure/IOP) and contains the ciliary muscle which controls accommodation (focusing ability).

================================================================================
Question 682 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Important function of iris is to:

Options:
  Divide eye into anterior and posterior segments
  Helps in crystalline lens accommodation
✓ Divide eye into anterior and posterior chamber
  Both b and c

Explanation:
The iris acts as a diaphragm, regulating light entry, and anatomically divides the anterior segment of the eye into the anterior chamber and the posterior chamber.

================================================================================
Question 683 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The most common primarily intraocular malignancy in adults is:

Options:
  Retinoblastoma
✓ Choroidal Melanoma
  Squamous cell carcinoma of conjunctiva
  Iris naevus

Explanation:
Uveal melanoma (specifically Choroidal Melanoma) is the most common primary intraocular malignant tumor in adults. Retinoblastoma is the most common in children.

================================================================================
Question 684 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Number of layers in neurosensory retina is:

Options:
✓ 10
  11
  12

Explanation:
The retina has 10 layers in total. The neurosensory retina specifically refers to the inner 9 layers (excluding the RPE). However, standard text questions often ask for total layers which is 10. If the option 9 is missing, usually 10 is the intended answer for layers of retina.

================================================================================
Question 685 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In retinal detachment, fluid accumulates between:

Options:
  Outer plexiform layer and inner nuclear layer
✓ Neurosensory retina and layer of retinal pigment epithelium
  Nerve fiber layer
  Retinal pigment epithelium and Bruch's membrane

Explanation:
Retinal detachment is the separation of the neurosensory retina from the underlying Retinal Pigment Epithelium (RPE).

================================================================================
Question 686 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A young patient with sudden pain loss of vision, with systolic murmur and ocular examination reveal a cherry red spot with clear AC, the likely diagnosis is:

Options:
✓ Central Retinal Artery Occlusion
  Central Vein Occlusion
  Diabetes Mellitus
  Branch

Explanation:
Cherry red spot indicates CRAO. The systolic murmur suggests an embolic source (e.g., valves).

  Microaneurysm
  Retinal hemorrhage
  Retinal detachment

Diabetic Macular Edema (DME) is the most common cause of visual impairment in diabetic retinopathy.

Question 688 (WMC - 2023)

In retinitis pigmentosa, the pigmentation in retina starts at:

✓ Equator
  At the disc

Pigmentation (bone spicules) in RP typically starts in the mid-periphery (equatorial region).

================================================================================
Question 689 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In CRAO, a cherry red spot is due to:

Options:
  Hemorrhage at macula
  Increased choroidal perfusion
  Increased in retinal perfusion at macula
✓ The contrast between pale retina and reddish intact choriocapillaris

Explanation:
The retina becomes oedematous and opaque (white) due to ischemia, except at the foveola where it is very thin. The red color of the underlying choroid shows through this thin area, creating the 'cherry red spot' contrast.

The average axial length is approximately 24 mm.

  Meningioma

Question 693 (WMC - 2023)

All cranial orbit passes through the superior orbit fissure except:

Options:
✓ 8TH
  4th
  3rd

Explanation:
CN III, IV, and VI pass through the SOF. CN VIII (Vestibulocochlear) does not enter the orbit.

Question 694 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A four-year-old boy is seen in emergency department with an 8mm of laceration in upper lid nod involving the lid margin. He says that he injured his eye on the corner of the table. He has mild ptosis on the left side and there is herniation of the orbital fat through the laceration. The eye examination is normal. Which of the following is next MOST appropriate step:

Options:
✓ CT of the Orbit
  Glue the laceration
  MRI of the Orbit
  Ultrasound the Orbit

Explanation:
Herniation of fat indicates the orbital septum is breached. In a child, especially with an upper lid laceration, one must rule out a penetrating orbital injury or intracranial extension (roof fracture) with a CT scan before repair.

  Zygomatic ( lateral wall)
  Lachrymal (medial wall)
  Frontal (roof)

  Patching the eye
  Instilling a drop of eye in the eye

  Instilling a drop of surface anesthetic into the eye

Question 698 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
In Myopia:

Options:
✓ Length of eye ball is short
  Corneal radius of curvature is less
  Lens is less spherical
  Image forms in front of retina when the patient accommodates

Explanation:
In myopia, the eyeball is too long or the cornea is too steep (curvature greater/radius less). The image forms *in front* of the retina.

Question 699 (WMC - 2023)

All of the following are extraocular muscle of eye except:

Options:
  Superior rectus
✓ Ciliary Muscle
  Inferior Oblique
  Superior oblique

Explanation:
Ciliary muscle is an intraocular muscle (smooth muscle). The others are extraocular muscles.

Question 700 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
The action of inferior Oblique is:

Options:
  Depression, extorsion, abduction
  Depression, extorsion, adduction
  Elevation, extorsion, adduction
✓ Elevation, extorsion, abduction

Explanation:
The Inferior Oblique elevates, extorts, and abducts the eye.

================================================================================
Question 701 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In paralytic squint, the difference between primary and secondary deviation in the gaze of the paralytic muscle:

Options:
✓ Increases
  Decreases
  Remains the same
  None

Explanation:
In paralytic squint, secondary deviation (when the paretic eye fixates) is greater than primary deviation (when the normal eye fixates) due to Hering's Law.

================================================================================
Question 702 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Paralytic ectropion occurs in:

Options:
  Third never paralysis
  Trigeminal never paralys
✓ Facial never paralysis
  Trochlear never paralysis

Explanation:
Facial nerve (CN VII) paralysis causes weakness of the orbicularis oculi, leading to paralytic ectropion.

================================================================================
Question 703 (WMC - 2024)
================================================================================

Question:
The main manifestation of antrochoanal polyp is:

Options:
  Proptosis.
✓ Unilateral nasal obstruction.
  Headache.
  Sneezing.

Explanation:
An antrochoanal polyp typically grows posteriorly from the maxillary sinus into the choana and nasopharynx, causing marked unilateral nasal obstruction, often on expiration.

================================================================================
Question 704 (WMC - 2024)
================================================================================

Question:
Nasopharyngeal carcinoma cause Horner's syndrome as a result of infiltration of:

Options:
  cranial nerve.
  5th cranial nerve.
  7th cranial nerve.
✓ Cervical sympathetic chain.

Explanation:
Horner's syndrome (ptosis, miosis, anhidrosis) results from the interruption of the sympathetic nerve supply. In nasopharyngeal carcinoma, this occurs due to infiltration of the cervical sympathetic chain, typically in the parapharyngeal space or near the carotid sheath.

================================================================================
Question 705 (WMC - 2024)
================================================================================

Question:
Inability to raise the eye brow & close the same eye with deviation of the angle of the mouth to the opposite side is:

Options:
  UMNL 7th cranial nerve palsy.
  UMNL 5th cranial nerve palsy.
  LMNL 5th cranial nerve palsy.
✓ LMNL 7th cranial nerve palsy.

Explanation:
Inability to raise the eyebrow (forehead sparing is absent) and close the eye indicates involvement of the entire side of the face, which is characteristic of a Lower Motor Neuron Lesion (LMNL) of the facial nerve (7th CN). In UMNL, the forehead is spared.
